## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the rate law dA/dt as a function of concentration A and time t. In chemical kinetics, rate laws typically express dA/dt as functions of concentration raised to various powers (reaction orders), possibly with time-dependent terms for non-elementary or externally driven reactions.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Zero-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 (constant rate, independent of concentration)
- First-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A (radioactive decay, unimolecular decomposition)
- Second-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**2 (bimolecular reaction of single species)
- Fractional/general n-th order: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 (empirical rate law with non-integer order)
- Mixed-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 * A**2 (parallel first and second order pathways)
- Reversible first-order: dA_dt = c0 * A + c1 (forward and reverse reaction with equilibrium)
- Michaelis-Menten type: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A) (enzyme-catalyzed or saturation kinetics)
- Autocatalytic reaction: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (logistic-type autocatalysis, A reacts with product)
- Inhibition kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A / (c1 + A**2) (substrate inhibition)
- Time-dependent decay rate: dA_dt = c0 * A * exp(c1 * t) (time-varying rate coefficient)
- Cooperative kinetics (Hill-type): dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 / (c2 + A**c1) (cooperative binding/reaction)
- Third-order kinetics: dA_dt = c0 * A**3 (termolecular or empirical third-order reaction)
- Combined zero and first order: dA_dt = c0 + c1 * A + c2 * A**2 (polynomial rate law expansion)
- Power-law with time modulation: dA_dt = c0 * A**c1 * t**c2 (fractal or dispersive kinetics)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- If dA/dt is proportional to A^n, plotting log|dA/dt| vs log|A| should yield a straight line with slope n (reaction order determination)
- If dA/dt depends only on A and not on t, the system is autonomous and the rate law is a pure function of concentration
- Negative values of dA/dt with positive A suggest a consumption/decay reaction; the sign of the rate constant encodes reaction direction
- Saturation in rate at high A suggests enzyme-like or surface-catalyzed kinetics with a Michaelis-Menten denominator structure
- A rate law of form A*(c-A) indicates autocatalysis where the product catalyzes the reaction, producing sigmoidal concentration-time profiles
- Explicit time dependence in the rate law may indicate photolysis, temperature ramps, or catalyst deactivation over time
- If dA/dt vs A shows a parabolic shape, this suggests competing first and second order mechanisms (quadratic in A)
- A rate that approaches zero as A approaches a nonzero value suggests a reversible reaction with equilibrium concentration offset
